كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها باب القبول وعدمه أو يبول على الطريق، أو يأكل فيه، أو يظهر سبَّ السَّلف ۵۷۷ (أو يبول على الطريق ، أو يأكل فيه ، أو يظهر سب) السلف) : أي الصحابة، والعلماء المجتهدين الماضين رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين. [١]قوله : أو يبول ... الخ ؛ أي لا تقبل الشهادة منه ؛ لأنه تارك للمروءة، فإذا كان لا يستحي من مثل ذلك لا يمتنع عن الكذب، فيتهم، وكذا كل من يأكل في السوق بين الناس. تکه وقال في «النهاية»: إذا شرب الماء، أو أكل الفول على الطريق لا يقدح في عدالته ؛ لأنَّ الناس لا تستقبحُ ذلك. انتهى. والمراد بالبول على الطريق إذا كان بحيث يراه الناس ، وكذا لا تقبل شهادة النخاس، وهو الدَّلال، إلا إذا كان عدلاً لا يحلف ولا يكذب. كذا في «السراج الوهاج». ومثله الذي يكشف عورته ليستنجي من جانب البركة، والناس حضور، وقد كثر في زماننا. كذا في «المنح ) ، بخلاف كشفها للبول والغائط إذا لم يجد ما يستتر به ؛ فإنّه لا يفسق به، ذكره الطحطاوي نقلاً. عن أبي السعود [۲] قوله : أو يظهر سب السلف ؛ فلا تقبل شهادته ؛ لظهور فسقه ، قيَّد بالظهور ؛ لأنه لو كتمه تقبل. كذا في «الهداية (٥). قال في «العناية ) : روى ابن سماعة له عن أبي يوسف له أنه قال : لا أقبل شهادة من سب أصحاب رسول الله وأقبل شهادة من يتبرؤ منهم، وفرَّقوا بأنَّ إظهاره
Book of testimony and retraction, chapter on acceptance and non-acceptance. Or he urinates on the road, or eats on it, or manifests slandering the predecessors. (Or he urinates on the road, or eats on it, or manifests slandering) the predecessors: meaning the Companions and the past mujtahid scholars, may Allah be pleased with them all. [1] His saying: 'or he urinates... etc.'; i.e., his testimony is not accepted because he abandons dignity (murua). If he is not ashamed of such, he does not refrain from lying, so he is suspected. Similarly, everyone who eats in the marketplace among people. And it is said in al-Nihaya: if he drinks water or eats beans on the road, it does not impugn his integrity because people do not consider that reprehensible. End. And what is meant by urinating on the road is if he does so where people see him. Similarly, the testimony of a broker (nakhkhas) is not accepted unless he is upright and does not swear oaths or lie. So in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And similarly, one who exposes his private parts to perform istinja by the side of a pool while people are present, and this has become common in our time. So in al-Manh. Unlike exposing them for urination or defecation if he does not find something to conceal himself, for he does not become a transgressor by that. Al-Tahtawi mentioned it quoting from Abu al-Suud. [2] His saying: Or he manifests slandering the predecessors: his testimony is not accepted because of his manifest transgression. He restricted it to manifestation because if he conceals it, it is accepted. So in al-Hidaya. He said in al-Inaya: Ibn Samaa narrated from Abu Yusuf that he said: I do not accept the testimony of one who slanders the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, and I accept the testimony of one who dissociates from them. And they differentiated by saying that his manifestation [of slander is worse].
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on acceptance of testimony lists actions that disqualify a witness. First, urinating or eating on a public road in a way that people see demonstrates a lack of shame (muru'a) and thus the person is suspected of being untruthful. However, the commentary clarifies that minor acts like drinking water or eating beans are not considered disgraceful, so they do not affect integrity. Similarly, exposing private parts for istinja is only problematic if done openly without necessity; if one has no cover, it is excused. Second, manifesting slander (sabb) of the Salaf—meaning the Companions and early mujtahid scholars—is clear transgression (fisq) and invalidates testimony. The key condition is 'manifestation': if one privately harbors such beliefs but does not express them, his testimony may still be accepted. The passage also notes a narration from Abu Yusuf who distinguishes between slanderers and those who merely dissociate (tabarru) from the Companions, accepting the latter's testimony.

Key Terms
المروءة (al-muru'a): Decency, dignity, and social propriety that prevents one from committing disgraceful acts.
السلف (al-salaf): The predecessors, specifically the Companions and the early mujtahid scholars.
السب (al-sabb): Verbal abuse or slander, speaking ill of someone in a way that defames them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for slandering the Salaf to disqualify a witness?
A) The witness must have heard it from others
B) The slander must be openly manifested
C) The slander must be written down
D) The slander must be repeated multiple times

Key Takeaway
Testimony is rejected for open shameless acts or manifest slander of the Salaf; concealment or minor acts preserve admissibility.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Disqualification of Witnesses: Public Indecency and Cursing the Salaf
Ruling with proof: disqualifying acts and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify acts that violate muru'a and explain why open cursing of the Salaf disqualifies a witness, distinguishing between public and private sin.

Core Idea
Open sin disqualifies a witness; concealment preserves probity.

Witnesses must possess 'adala (probity), which requires moral integrity (muru'a) and avoidance of major sin. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya examines two categories of disqualifying behavior: public indecency that shows lack of shame, and openly cursing the pious predecessors (al-Salaf). The key principle is that public manifestation of sin, not private belief, undermines reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Determine whether the witness's action falls under prohibited public indecency or cursing. For indecency, assess if the act is socially reprehensible (e.g., urinating in public view, eating in the market).
Minor acts like drinking water on the road do not disqualify according to al-Nihaya.
2
Evaluate Publicity
Check whether the act was done openly or in private. Openness is key: hidden sins do not affect probity because they do not indicate a pattern of shamelessness.
For cursing the Salaf, only open cursing (izhar) disqualifies; concealed cursing does not.
3
Apply the Ruling
If the act is public and violates muru'a or constitutes open fisq (sinfulness), the witness's testimony is rejected. If the act is private or not universally condemned, probity remains intact.
The hadith 'Insulting a Muslim is sinfulness' broadens the rule to any Muslim, not just the Salaf.
4
Consider Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Yusuf dissented: he accepts testimony from one who dissociates from the Companions (tabarra) but not from one who curses them, because cursing indicates foolishness.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) rejects testimony for open cursing, following Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها باب القبول وعدمه (أو يبول على الطريق، أو يأكل فيه، أو يظهر سبَّ السَّلف) (١) : أي الصحابة، والعلماء المجتهدين الماضين رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين. قوله : أو يبول ... الخ ؛ أي لا تقبل الشهادة منه ؛ لأنه تارك للمروءة، فإذا كان لا يستحي من مثل ذلك لا يمتنع عن الكذب، فيتهم، وكذا كل من يأكل في السوق بين الناس. وقال في «النهاية»: إذا شرب الماء، أو أكل الفول على الطريق لا يقدح في عدالته ؛ لأنَّ الناس لا تستقبحُ ذلك. انتهى. والمراد بالبول على الطريق إذا كان بحيث يراه الناس، وكذا لا تقبل شهادة النخاس، وهو الدَّلال، إلا إذا كان عدلاً لا يحلف ولا يكذب. كذا في «السراج الوهاج». ومثله الذي يكشف عورته ليستنجي من جانب البركة، والناس حضور، وقد كثر في زماننا. كذا في «المنح»، بخلاف كشفها للبول والغائط إذا لم يجد ما يستتر به؛ فإنّه لا يفسق به، ذكره الطحطاوي نقلاً. عن أبي السعود. قوله : أو يظهر سب السلف؛ فلا تقبل شهادته؛ لظهور فسقه، قيَّد بالظهور؛ لأنه لو كتمه تقبل. كذا في «الهداية». قال في «العناية»: روى ابن سماعة له عن أبي يوسف له أنه قال: لا أقبل شهادة من سب أصحاب رسول الله وأقبل شهادة من يتبرؤ منهم، وفرَّقوا بأنَّ إظهاره سفه لا يأتي به إلا الأسقاط السخفة، وشهادة السخيف لا تقبل، ولا كذلك المتبرئ؛ لأنه يعتقد ديناً وإن كان على باطل، فلم يظهر فسقه. كذا في «المنح». والسب: - بتشديد الباء -، هو التكلّم في عرض الإنسان بما يعيبه. كذا في «جامع الرموز»، والسلف: جمع سالف، وهو الماضي، وفي الشرع: اسم لكلِّ من يقلد مذهبه ويقتفى أثره كأبي حنيفة الله وأصحابه، فإنهم سلفنا، والصحابة والتابعونَ سلف لأبي حنيفة الله وأصحابه. كذا في «الكفاية» ناقلا عن بدر الدين. وذكر في «البحر»: إِنَّ السلف الصالح الصدرُ الأول من التابعين، والخلف: بفتح اللام ومن بعدهم، فهي الخير وبالسكون في الشر، وإنما قيَّده بالسَّلَف تبعاً لكلامهم، وإلا فالأولى أن يقال أو يظهر سب مسلم؛ لأنَّ العدالة تسقط بسب المسلم، وإن لم يكن من السلف؛ لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (سباب المسلم فسوق وقتاله كفر).
The book of testimony and retracting from it. Chapter of acceptance and non-acceptance. (Or he urinates on the road, or eats in it, or openly curses the Salaf) (1): i.e. the Companions and the past mujtahid scholars, may Allah be pleased with them all. His saying: 'or urinates... etc.': i.e. his testimony is not accepted because he has abandoned moral integrity (muru'a). If he is not ashamed of such, he will not refrain from lying, so he is accused. Similarly, anyone who eats in the market among people. And it is said in al-Nihaya: if he drinks water or eats beans on the road, it does not impugn his probity because people do not find that reprehensible. End. And what is meant by urinating on the road is when he can be seen by people. Similarly, the testimony of a broker (nakhkhas) is not accepted unless he is upright and does not swear or lie. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And likewise, one who uncovers his private parts to clean himself at the edge of a pool while people are present, and this has become common in our time. Thus in al-Minh. Contrary to uncovering them for urination and defecation if he cannot find anything to screen himself; then he does not become sinful, mentioned by al-Tahtawi narrating from Abu al-Su'ud. His saying: 'or openly curses the Salaf': so his testimony is not accepted due to the manifestation of his sinfulness. He restricted it to 'openly' because if he conceals it, it is accepted. Thus in al-Hidaya. He said in al-‘Inaya: Ibn Sama'a narrated from Abu Yusuf that he said: I do not accept the testimony of one who curses the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, but I accept the testimony of one who dissociates from them (tabarra). And they distinguished: because its public display is foolishness that only the lowly and foolish do, and the testimony of a foolish person is not accepted. But the one who dissociates is not like that, because he believes it to be a religion even if false, so his sinfulness has not manifested. Thus in al-Minh. And 'sabb' with tashdid of the ba is speaking about a person's reputation with what defames him. Thus in Jami' al-Rumuz. And 'salaf' is the plural of 'salif' meaning past, and in sacred law it is a name for everyone who follows his madhhab and emulates his path, like Abu Hanifa and his companions, for they are our Salaf, and the Companions and Successors are the Salaf for Abu Hanifa and his companions. Thus in al-Kifaya, quoting from Badr al-Din. And it is mentioned in al-Bahr that the righteous Salaf are the first generation from the Successors, and the Khalaf (with fatha on the lam) are those after them, so it is good, and with sukun it is evil. He only restricted it to Salaf following their terminology, otherwise it would be better to say 'or openly curses a Muslim' because probity is removed by cursing a Muslim even if not from the Salaf, due to his saying peace be upon him: 'Insulting a Muslim is sinfulness and fighting him is disbelief.'
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage discusses two categories of actions that disqualify a witness in Hanafi law. First, acts that violate moral integrity (muru'a) such as urinating on the road in public, eating in the marketplace, or uncovering private parts for cleaning in front of people. The rationale is that lack of shame leads to dishonest testimony. However, minor acts not considered distasteful by society, like drinking water or eating beans, do not affect probity. Second, openly cursing the Salaf (pious predecessors including the Companions and early scholars) disqualifies a witness because it indicates clear sinfulness. The text highlights that concealment of such cursing does not disqualify, as the sin is private. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: Abu Yusuf accepts testimony from one who dissociates from the Companions but not from one who curses, because cursing demonstrates foolishness. The author also suggests that the rule should apply to cursing any Muslim, as per the hadith that insulting a Muslim is sin. The overall principle is that a witness must have probity ('adala), and any public display of sin or moral deficiency voids it.

Key Terms
السلف (al-salaf): Pious predecessors: the Companions, Successors, and early mujtahid imams such as Abu Hanifa and his companions.
المروءة (al-muru'a): Moral integrity and decency; a quality required for probity ('adala). Publicly indecent acts (urinating, eating on road) violate it.
السب (al-sabb): Speaking about a person's honor in a defamatory manner; cursing or insulting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a witness's testimony rejected if he openly curses the Salaf?
A) Because cursing is a major sin that removes probity regardless of openness.
B) Because open cursing indicates his sinfulness and foolishness, making him unreliable.
C) Because the Salaf are not to be mentioned at all in testimony.
D) Because the witness must be a descendant of the Salaf.

Key Takeaway
Public indecency and open cursing of the Salaf disqualify a witness because they manifest sinfulness, destroying probity; private sins do not affect testimony.
